</table>
<p><b>Nebraska</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'b' in 'buy'">b</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Nebraska.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/En-us-Nebraska.ogg" title="En-us-Nebraska.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span> is a <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> that lies in both the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">Midwestern United States</a>. The state is bordered by <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> to the southeast, both across the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> to the southwest and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> to the west. It is the only <a href="/wiki/List_of_landlocked_U.S._states#Triply_landlocked" title="List of landlocked U.S. states">triply landlocked U.S. state</a>. Nebraska's area is just over 77,220 sq mi (200,000 km<sup>2</sup>) with almost 1.9 million people. Its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_capital" title="State capital">state capital</a> is <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln</a>, and its largest city is <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a>, which is on the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a>.</p>
<p>Indigenous peoples including <a href="/wiki/Omaha_people" title="Omaha people">Omaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouria" title="Missouria">Missouria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponca" title="Ponca">Ponca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pawnee_people" title="Pawnee people">Pawnee</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otoe_tribe" title="Otoe tribe">Otoe</a>, and various branches of the <a href="/wiki/Lakota_people" title="Lakota people">Lakota</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sioux" title="Sioux">Sioux</a>) tribes lived in the region for thousands of years before European exploration. The state is crossed by many historic trails and was explored by the <a href="/wiki/Lewis_and_Clark_Expedition" title="Lewis and Clark Expedition">Lewis and Clark Expedition</a>.</p>
<p>Nebraska was admitted as the 37th state of the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> in 1867. It is the only state in the United States whose legislature is <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> and officially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonpartisan_system" title="Nonpartisan system">nonpartisan</a>.</p>
<p>Nebraska is composed of two major land regions: the <a href="/wiki/Dissected_Till_Plains" title="Dissected Till Plains">Dissected Till Plains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. The Dissected Till Plains is a region of gently rolling hills and contains the state's largest cities, Omaha and Lincoln. The Great Plains occupy most of western Nebraska, characterized by treeless <a href="/wiki/Prairie" title="Prairie">prairie</a>, suitable for cattle-grazing. The state has a large agriculture sector and is a major producer of beef, pork, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a>. There are two major climatic zones: the eastern half of the state has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa</i>), with a unique warmer subtype considered "warm-temperate" near the southern plains like in Kansas and Oklahoma which have a predominantly <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Humid_subtropical" title="Humid subtropical">humid subtropical</a> climate. The western half has a primarily <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (Koppen <i>BSk</i>). The state has wide variations between winter and summer temperatures, decreasing south through the state. Violent <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">thunderstorms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> occur primarily during spring and summer, but sometimes in autumn. Chinook winds tend to warm the state significantly in the winter and early spring.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nebraska's name is derived from transliteration of the archaic <a href="/wiki/Chiwere_language" title="Chiwere language">Otoe</a> words <i>Ñí Brásge</i>, pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ɲĩbɾasꜜkɛ]</a></span> (contemporary Otoe <i>Ñí Bráhge</i>), or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Omaha-Ponca_language" title="Omaha-Ponca language">Omaha</a> <i>Ní Btháska</i>, pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[nĩbɫᶞasꜜka]</a></span>, meaning "flat water", after the <a href="/wiki/Platte_River" title="Platte River">Platte River</a> that flows through the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nebraska" title="History of Nebraska">History of Nebraska</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_1718.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="497" data-file-width="634" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nebraska_1718.jpg/220px-Nebraska_1718.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nebraska_1718.jpg/330px-Nebraska_1718.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Nebraska_1718.jpg/440px-Nebraska_1718.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_1718.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nebraska in 1718, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guillaume_de_L%27Isle" title="Guillaume de L'Isle">Guillaume de L'Isle</a> map, with the approximate area of the future state highlighted.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">Indigenous peoples</a> lived in the region of present-day Nebraska for thousands of years before European exploration. The historic tribes in the state included the <a href="/wiki/Omaha_people" title="Omaha people">Omaha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Missouria" title="Missouria">Missouria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ponca" title="Ponca">Ponca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pawnee_people" title="Pawnee people">Pawnee</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otoe_tribe" title="Otoe tribe">Otoe</a>, and various branches of the <a href="/wiki/Lakota_people" title="Lakota people">Lakota</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sioux" title="Sioux">Sioux</a>), some of which migrated from eastern areas into this region. When European exploration, trade, and settlement began, both Spain and France sought to control the region. In the 1690s, Spain established trade connections with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apache_people" title="Apache people">Apaches</a>, whose territory then included western Nebraska. By 1703, France had developed a regular trade with the native peoples along the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a> in Nebraska, and by 1719 had signed treaties with several of these peoples. After war broke out between the two countries, Spain dispatched an armed expedition to Nebraska under <a href="/wiki/Villasur_expedition" title="Villasur expedition">Lieutenant General Pedro de Villasur</a> in 1720. The party was attacked and destroyed near present-day <a href="/wiki/Columbus,_Nebraska" title="Columbus, Nebraska">Columbus</a> by a large force of Pawnees and Otoes, both allied to the French. The massacre ended Spanish exploration of the area for the remainder of the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hanson_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-hanson-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1762, during the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a>, France ceded the Louisiana territory to Spain. This left Britain and Spain competing for dominance along the Mississippi; by 1773, the British were trading with the native peoples of Nebraska. In response, Spain dispatched two trading expeditions up the Missouri in 1794 and 1795; the second, under James Mackay, established the first European settlement in Nebraska near the mouth of the Platte. Later that year, Mackay's party built a trading post, dubbed Fort Carlos IV (Fort Charles), near present-day <a href="/wiki/Homer,_Nebraska" title="Homer, Nebraska">Homer</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hanson_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-hanson-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lociana_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-lociana-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-charles_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-charles-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1819, the United States established <a href="/wiki/Fort_Atkinson_(Nebraska)" title="Fort Atkinson (Nebraska)">Fort Atkinson</a> as the first U.S. Army post west of the Missouri River, just east of present-day <a href="/wiki/Fort_Calhoun,_Nebraska" title="Fort Calhoun, Nebraska">Fort Calhoun</a>. The army abandoned the fort in 1827 as migration moved further west. European-American settlement was scarce until 1848 and the <a href="/wiki/California_Gold_Rush" title="California Gold Rush">California Gold Rush</a>. On May 30, 1854, the US Congress created the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Territory" title="Nebraska Territory">Nebraska</a> territories, divided by the <a href="/wiki/40th_parallel_north" title="40th parallel north">Parallel 40° North</a>, under the <a href="/wiki/Kansas%E2%80%93Nebraska_Act" title="Kansas–Nebraska Act">Kansas–Nebraska Act</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Establishment_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Establishment-12">[12]</a></sup> The Nebraska Territory included parts of the current states of <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montana" title="Montana">Montana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> The territorial capital of Nebraska was <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1668" data-file-width="2100" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg/220px-00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg/330px-00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg/440px-00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:00DI0943_-_Flickr_-_USDAgov.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Homestead_Acts" title="Homestead Acts">Homesteaders</a> in central Nebraska in 1888.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the 1860s, after the U.S. government forced many of the Native American tribes to cede their lands and settle on <a href="/wiki/Indian_reservation" title="Indian reservation">reservations</a>, it opened large tracts of land to agricultural development by Europeans and Americans. Under the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Homestead_Act" title="Homestead Act">Homestead Act</a>, thousands of settlers migrated into Nebraska to claim free land granted by the federal government. Because so few trees grew on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prairies" title="Prairies">prairies</a>, many of the first farming settlers built their <a href="/wiki/Sod_house" title="Sod house">homes of sod</a>, as had the Native Americans such as the Omaha. The first wave of settlement gave the territory a sufficient population to apply for statehood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Nebraska became the 37th state on March 1, 1867, and the capital was moved from Omaha to the center at Lancaster, later renamed <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln</a> after the recently assassinated President of the United States, <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>. The battle of <a href="/wiki/Massacre_Canyon" title="Massacre Canyon">Massacre Canyon</a> on August 5, 1873, was the last major battle between the <a href="/wiki/Pawnee_people" title="Pawnee people">Pawnee</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Sioux" title="Sioux">Sioux</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the 1870s to the 1880s, Nebraska experienced a large growth in population. Several factors contributed to attracting new residents. The first was that the vast prairie land was perfect for cattle grazing. This helped settlers to learn the unfamiliar geography of the area. The second factor was the invention of several farming technologies. Agricultural inventions such as barbed wire, wind mills, and the steel plow, combined with good weather, enabled settlers to use of Nebraska as prime farming land. By the 1880s, Nebraska's population had soared to more than 450,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Arbor_Day" title="Arbor Day">Arbor Day</a> holiday was founded in <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_City,_Nebraska" title="Nebraska City, Nebraska">Nebraska City</a> by territorial governor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J._Sterling_Morton" title="J. Sterling Morton">J. Sterling Morton</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Arbor_Day_Foundation" title="National Arbor Day Foundation">National Arbor Day Foundation</a> is still headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_City,_Nebraska" title="Nebraska City, Nebraska">Nebraska City</a>, with some offices in Lincoln.</p>
<p>In the late 19th century, many African Americans migrated from the South to Nebraska as part of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Migration_(African_American)" title="Great Migration (African American)">Great Migration</a>, primarily to Omaha which offered working class jobs in <a href="/wiki/Meat_packing_industry" title="Meat packing industry">meat packing</a>, the railroads and other industries. Omaha has a long history of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Civil_Rights_Movement_in_Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Civil Rights Movement in Omaha, Nebraska">civil rights</a> activism. Blacks encountered discrimination from other Americans in Omaha and especially from recent European immigrants, ethnic whites who were competing for the same jobs. In 1912, African Americans founded the Omaha chapter of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Colored_People" title="National Association for the Advancement of Colored People">National Association for the Advancement of Colored People</a> to work for improved conditions in the city and state.</p>
<p>Since the 1960s, <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a> activism in the state has increased, both through open protest, activities to build alliances with state and local governments, and in the slower, more extensive work of building tribal institutions and infrastructure. Native Americans in federally recognized tribes have pressed for self-determination, sovereignty and recognition. They have created community schools to preserve their cultures, as well as <a href="/wiki/Tribal_colleges_and_universities" title="Tribal colleges and universities">tribal colleges and universities</a>. Tribal politicians have also collaborated with state and county officials on regional issues.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Animation begins with a wide view of the entire United States and then zooms down to an area in Nebraska where water usage studies have been carried out.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The state is bordered by <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a> to the north; <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">Missouri</a> to the southeast, across the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_River" title="Missouri River">Missouri River</a>; <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> to the south; <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> to the southwest; and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> to the west. The state has <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Nebraska" title="List of counties in Nebraska">93 counties</a>; it occupies the central portion of the <a href="/wiki/Frontier_Strip" title="Frontier Strip">Frontier Strip</a>. Nebraska is split into two <a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">time zones</a>, with the state's eastern half observing <a href="/wiki/Central_Time_Zone" title="Central Time Zone">Central Time</a> and the western half observing <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Time_Zone" title="Mountain Time Zone">Mountain Time</a>. Three rivers cross the state from west to east. The <a href="/wiki/Platte_River" title="Platte River">Platte River</a>, formed by the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte</a> and the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte_River" title="South Platte River">South Platte</a>, runs through the state's central portion, the <a href="/wiki/Niobrara_River" title="Niobrara River">Niobrara River</a> flows through the northern part, and the <a href="/wiki/Republican_River" title="Republican River">Republican River</a> runs across the southern part.</p>
<p>Nebraska is composed of two major land regions: the <a href="/wiki/Dissected_Till_Plains" title="Dissected Till Plains">Dissected Till Plains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. The easternmost portion of the state was scoured by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ice_Age" title="Ice Age">Ice Age</a> <a href="/wiki/Glacier" title="Glacier">glaciers</a>; the Dissected Till Plains were left after the glaciers retreated. The Dissected Till Plains is a region of gently rolling hills; <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln</a> are in this region. The Great Plains occupy most of western Nebraska, with the region consisting of several smaller, diverse land regions, including the <a href="/wiki/Sandhills_(Nebraska)" title="Sandhills (Nebraska)">Sandhills</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pine_Ridge_(region)" title="Pine Ridge (region)">Pine Ridge</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Rainwater_Basin" title="Rainwater Basin">Rainwater Basin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wildcat_Hills" title="Wildcat Hills">Wildcat Hills</a>. <a href="/wiki/Panorama_Point" title="Panorama Point">Panorama Point</a>, at 5,424 feet (1,653 m), is Nebraska's highest point; though despite its name and elevation, it is a relatively low rise near the <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> borders. A past Nebraska tourism slogan was "Where the West Begins"; locations given for the beginning of the "West" include the Missouri River, the intersection of 13th and O Streets in Lincoln (where it is marked by a red brick star), the <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_west" title="100th meridian west">100th meridian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chimney_Rock_National_Historic_Site" title="Chimney Rock National Historic Site">Chimney Rock</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_land_management">Federal land management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Federal land management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Areas under the management of the <a href="/wiki/National_Park_Service" title="National Park Service">National Park Service</a> include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agate_Fossil_Beds_National_Monument" title="Agate Fossil Beds National Monument">Agate Fossil Beds National Monument</a> near <a href="/wiki/Harrison,_Nebraska" title="Harrison, Nebraska">Harrison</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/California_National_Historic_Trail" title="California National Historic Trail">California National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chimney_Rock_National_Historic_Site" title="Chimney Rock National Historic Site">Chimney Rock National Historic Site</a> near <a href="/wiki/Bayard,_Nebraska" title="Bayard, Nebraska">Bayard</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Homestead_National_Monument_of_America" title="Homestead National Monument of America">Homestead National Monument of America</a> in <a href="/wiki/Beatrice,_Nebraska" title="Beatrice, Nebraska">Beatrice</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lewis_%26_Clark_National_Historic_Trail" title="Lewis &amp; Clark National Historic Trail">Lewis &amp; Clark National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Missouri_National_Recreational_River" title="Missouri National Recreational River">Missouri National Recreational River</a> near <a href="/wiki/Ponca,_Nebraska" title="Ponca, Nebraska">Ponca</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mormon_Pioneer_National_Historic_Trail" title="Mormon Pioneer National Historic Trail">Mormon Pioneer National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Niobrara_National_Scenic_River" title="Niobrara National Scenic River">Niobrara National Scenic River</a> near <a href="/wiki/Valentine,_Nebraska" title="Valentine, Nebraska">Valentine</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oregon_National_Historic_Trail" title="Oregon National Historic Trail">Oregon National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pony_Express_National_Historic_Trail" title="Pony Express National Historic Trail">Pony Express National Historic Trail</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scotts_Bluff_National_Monument" title="Scotts Bluff National Monument">Scotts Bluff National Monument</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gering,_Nebraska" title="Gering, Nebraska">Gering</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Areas under the management of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Forest_Service" title="National Forest Service">National Forest Service</a> include:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nebraska_National_Forest" title="Nebraska National Forest">Nebraska National Forest</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oglala_National_Grassland" title="Oglala National Grassland">Oglala National Grassland</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_R._McKelvie_National_Forest" title="Samuel R. McKelvie National Forest">Samuel R. McKelvie National Forest</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NE_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1134" data-file-width="1440" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/NE_koppen.svg/220px-NE_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/NE_koppen.svg/330px-NE_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/NE_koppen.svg/440px-NE_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NE_koppen.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Köppen climate types in Nebraska</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1536" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg/220px-ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg/330px-ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg/440px-ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ScottsBluffNatMon_2002.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Winter at <a href="/wiki/Scotts_Bluff_National_Monument" title="Scotts Bluff National Monument">Scotts Bluff National Monument</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Two major climatic zones are represented in Nebraska: the eastern half of the state has a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfa</i>), and the western half, a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (Koppen <i>BSk</i>). The entire state experiences wide seasonal variations in temperature and precipitation. Average temperatures are fairly uniform across Nebraska, with hot summers and generally cold winters.</p>
<p>Average annual precipitation decreases east to west from about 31.5 inches (800 mm) in the southeast corner of the state to about 13.8 inches (350 mm) in the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Panhandle" title="Nebraska Panhandle">Panhandle</a>. Humidity also decreases significantly from east to west. Snowfall across the state is fairly even, with most of Nebraska receiving between 25 and 35 inches (65 and 90 cm) of snow annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Nebraska's highest recorded temperature is 118 °F (48 °C) at <a href="/wiki/Minden,_Nebraska" title="Minden, Nebraska">Minden</a> on July 24, 1936 and the lowest recorded temperature is −47 °F (−44 °C) at <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Camp_Clarke,_Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Camp Clarke, Nebraska (page does not exist)">Camp Clarke</a> on February 12, 1899.</p>
<p>Nebraska is in <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>. <a href="/wiki/Thunderstorm" title="Thunderstorm">Thunderstorms</a> are common in the spring and summer months, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severe_thunderstorm" title="Severe thunderstorm">violent thunderstorms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tornado" title="Tornado">tornadoes</a> happen primarily during the spring and summer, though they can also occur in the autumn. The <a href="/wiki/Chinook_wind" title="Chinook wind">chinook winds</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> provide a temporary moderating effect on temperatures in western Nebraska during the winter months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<table class="wikitable sortable" style="margin:auto;">

<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates that the population of Nebraska was 1,896,190 on July 1, 2015, a 3.82% increase since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PopEstUS_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-PopEstUS-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Center_of_population" title="Center of population">center of population</a> of Nebraska is in <a href="/wiki/Polk_County,_Nebraska" title="Polk County, Nebraska">Polk County</a>, in the city of <a href="/wiki/Shelby,_Nebraska" title="Shelby, Nebraska">Shelby</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ancestry">Ancestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Ancestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 Census</a>, 86.1% of the population was White (82.1% <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_white" title="Non-Hispanic white">non-Hispanic white</a>), 4.5% was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_American" title="African American">Black</a> or African American, 1.0% American Indian and Alaska Native, 1.8% Asian, 0.1% Native Hawaiian and other Pacific Islander, 2.2% from two or more races. 9.2% of the total population was of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">Hispanic</a> or Latino origin (they may be of any race).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2004, the population of Nebraska included about 84,000 foreign-born residents (4.8% of the population).</p>

<p>The five largest ancestry groups in Nebraska are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_American" title="German American">German</a> (38.6%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Irish_American" title="Irish American">Irish</a> (12.4%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_American" title="English American">English</a> (9.6%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">Mexican</a> (8.7%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_American" title="Czech American">Czech</a> (5.5%).</p>
<p>Nebraska has the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czech_American" title="Czech American">Czech American</a> and non-Mormon <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_American" title="Danish American">Danish American</a> population (as a percentage of the total population) in the nation. <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German Americans</a> are the largest ancestry group in most of the state, particularly in the eastern counties. <a href="/wiki/Thurston_County,_Nebraska" title="Thurston County, Nebraska">Thurston County</a> (made up entirely of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Omaha_(tribe)" title="Omaha (tribe)">Omaha</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Winnebago_(tribe)" title="Winnebago (tribe)">Winnebago</a> reservations) has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Indians_in_the_United_States" title="American Indians in the United States">American Indian</a> majority, and <a href="/wiki/Butler_County,_Nebraska" title="Butler County, Nebraska">Butler County</a> is one of only two counties in the nation with a Czech-American plurality.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The religious affiliations of the people of Nebraska are:</p>
<ul>
<li>Christian – 90%
<ul>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">Catholic</a> – 28%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheran</a> – 16%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a> – 11%</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baptist" title="Baptist">Baptist</a> – 9%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a> – 4%</li>
<li>Other Protestant – 21%</li>
<li>Other Christian – 1%</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>Non-religious – 9%</li>
<li>Other religions – 1%</li>
</ul>
<p>The largest single denominations by number of adherents in 2010 were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> (372,838), the <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_Church%E2%80%93Missouri_Synod" title="Lutheran Church–Missouri Synod">Lutheran Church–Missouri Synod</a> (112,585), the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">Evangelical Lutheran Church in America</a> (110,110) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Methodist_Church" title="United Methodist Church">United Methodist Church</a> (109,283).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.thearda.com_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.thearda.com-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Birth_data">Birth data</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Birth data">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlement">Settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Eighty-nine percent of the cities in Nebraska have fewer than 3,000 people. Nebraska shares this characteristic with five other Midwestern states: <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dakota" title="North Dakota">North Dakota</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Dakota" title="South Dakota">South Dakota</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iowa" title="Iowa">Iowa</a>. Hundreds of towns have a population of fewer than 1,000. Regional population declines have forced many rural schools to consolidate.</p>
<p>Fifty-three of Nebraska's 93 counties reported declining populations between 1990 and 2000, ranging from a 0.06% loss (<a href="/wiki/Frontier_County,_Nebraska" title="Frontier County, Nebraska">Frontier County</a>) to a 17.04% loss (<a href="/wiki/Hitchcock_County,_Nebraska" title="Hitchcock County, Nebraska">Hitchcock County</a>).</p>
<p>More urbanized areas of the state have experienced substantial growth. In 2000, the city of <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a> had a population of 390,007; in 2005, the city's estimated population was 414,521 (427,872 including the recently annexed city of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elkhorn,_Nebraska" title="Elkhorn, Nebraska">Elkhorn</a>), a 6.3% increase over five years. The 2010 census showed that Omaha has a population of 408,958. The city of <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln</a> had a 2000 population of 225,581 and a 2010 population of 258,379, a 14.5% increase.</p>
<p>As of the 2010 Census, there were 530 cities and villages in the state of Nebraska. There are five classifications of cities and villages in Nebraska, which is based upon population. All population figures are 2013 <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">Census Bureau</a> estimates unless flagged by a reference number.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">

<p>Second Class Cities (800 – 4,999) and Villages (100–800) make up the rest of the communities in Nebraska. There are 116 second class cities and 382 villages in the state.</p>

<p><b>Other areas</b></p>
<ul>
<li>Grand Island, Hastings and Kearney comprise the "<a href="/wiki/Tri-Cities,_Nebraska" title="Tri-Cities, Nebraska">Tri-Cities</a>" area, with a combined population of 168,748</li>
<li>The northeast corner of Nebraska is part of the <a href="/wiki/Siouxland" title="Siouxland">Siouxland</a> region.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Nebraska has a <a href="/wiki/Progressive_tax" title="Progressive tax">progressive income tax</a>. The portion of income from $0 to $2,400 is taxed at 2.56%; from $2,400 to $17,500, at 3.57%; from $17,500 to $27,000, at 5.12%; and income over $27,000, at 6.84%. The standard deduction for a single taxpayer is $5,700; the personal exemption is $118.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nebraska has a state sales and use tax of 5.5%. In addition to the state tax, some Nebraska cities assess a city sales and use tax, in 0.5% increments, up to a maximum of 1.5%. <a href="/wiki/Dakota_County,_Nebraska" title="Dakota County, Nebraska">Dakota County</a> levies an additional 0.5% county sales tax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> Food and ingredients that are generally for home preparation and consumption are not taxable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> All <a href="/wiki/Real_property" title="Real property">real property</a> within the state of Nebraska is taxable unless specifically exempted by statute. Since 1992, only depreciable <a href="/wiki/Personal_property" title="Personal property">personal property</a> is subject to tax and all other personal property is exempt from tax. <a href="/wiki/Inheritance_tax" title="Inheritance tax">Inheritance tax</a> is collected at the county level.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nebraska_locations_by_per_capita_income" title="Nebraska locations by per capita income">Nebraska locations by per capita income</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2087" data-file-width="3195" height="144" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_grain_silo_RAAM_2015_by_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Nebraska grain bins and elevator</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Economic_Analysis" title="Bureau of Economic Analysis">Bureau of Economic Analysis</a> estimates of Nebraska's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_state_product" title="Gross state product">gross state product</a> in 2010 was $89.8 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_personal_income_in_the_United_States" title="Per capita personal income in the United States">Per capita personal income</a> in 2004 was $31,339, 25th in the nation. Nebraska has a large agriculture sector, and is a major producer of <a href="/wiki/Beef" title="Beef">beef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">pork</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn (maize)</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soybeans" title="Soybeans">soybeans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum_bicolor" title="Sorghum bicolor">sorghum</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Other important economic sectors include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freight" title="Freight">freight</a> transport (by rail and truck), <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">manufacturing</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telecommunications" title="Telecommunications">telecommunications</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Insurance" title="Insurance">insurance</a>.</p>
<p>As of April 2015, the state's <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a> rate was 2.5%, the lowest in the nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kool-Aid" title="Kool-Aid">Kool-Aid</a> was created in 1927 by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Perkins_(inventor)" title="Edwin Perkins (inventor)">Edwin Perkins</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Hastings,_Nebraska" title="Hastings, Nebraska">Hastings</a>, which celebrates the event the second weekend of every August with <a class="external text" href="http://www.kool-aiddays.com" rel="nofollow">Kool-Aid Days</a>, and Kool-Aid is the official soft drink of Nebraska.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/CliffsNotes" title="CliffsNotes">CliffsNotes</a></i> were developed by <a href="/wiki/Clifton_Hillegass" title="Clifton Hillegass">Clifton Hillegass</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rising_City,_Nebraska" title="Rising City, Nebraska">Rising City</a>. He adapted his pamphlets from the Canadian publications, <i><a href="/wiki/Coles_(bookstore)" title="Coles (bookstore)">Coles Notes</a></i>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a>, whose <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">Chief executive officer</a> (CEO), <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a>, was ranked in March 2009 by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> magazine as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_billionaires_(2009)" title="List of billionaires (2009)">second richest person in the world</a>. The city is also home to <a href="/wiki/Mutual_of_Omaha" title="Mutual of Omaha">Mutual of Omaha</a>, InfoUSA, <a href="/wiki/TD_Ameritrade" title="TD Ameritrade">TD Ameritrade</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Corporation" title="West Corporation">West Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valmont_Industries" title="Valmont Industries">Valmont Industries</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Woodmen_of_the_World" title="Woodmen of the World">Woodmen of the World</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kiewit_Corporation" title="Kiewit Corporation">Kiewit Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ameritas_Life_Insurance_Company" title="Ameritas Life Insurance Company">Ameritas Life Insurance Corp.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nelnet" title="Nelnet">Nelnet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandhills_Publishing_Company" title="Sandhills Publishing Company">Sandhills Publishing Company</a>, and Duncan Aviation are based in <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buckle_(store)" title="Buckle (store)">The Buckle</a> is based in <a href="/wiki/Kearney,_Nebraska" title="Kearney, Nebraska">Kearney</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sidney,_Nebraska" title="Sidney, Nebraska">Sidney</a> is the national headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Cabela%27s" title="Cabela's">Cabela's</a>, a specialty retailer of outdoor goods.</p>
<p>The world's largest <a href="/wiki/Rail_yard" title="Rail yard">train yard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bailey_Yard" title="Bailey Yard">Bailey Yard</a>, is in <a href="/wiki/North_Platte,_Nebraska" title="North Platte, Nebraska">North Platte</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Locking_pliers" title="Locking pliers">Vise-Grip</a> was invented by William Petersen in 1924, and was manufactured in <a href="/wiki/De_Witt,_Nebraska" title="De Witt, Nebraska">De Witt</a> until the plant was closed and moved to China in late 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lincoln's Kawasaki Motors Manufacturing is the only Kawasaki plant in the world to produce the <a href="/wiki/Jet_Ski" title="Jet Ski">Jet Ski</a>, <a href="/wiki/All-terrain_vehicle" title="All-terrain vehicle">All-terrain vehicle</a> (ATV), and Mule lines of product. The facility employs more than 1200 people.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Spade_Ranch_(Nebraska)" title="Spade Ranch (Nebraska)">Spade Ranch</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Sandhills_(Nebraska)" title="Sandhills (Nebraska)">Sandhills</a>, is one of Nebraska's oldest and largest beef cattle operations.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Railroads">Railroads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Railroads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nebraska_railroads" title="List of Nebraska railroads">List of Nebraska railroads</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a>, headquartered in Omaha, was incorporated on July 1, 1862, in the wake of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Railway_Acts" title="Pacific Railway Acts">Pacific Railway Act of 1862</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WDL_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-43">[43]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bailey_Yard" title="Bailey Yard">Bailey Yard</a>, in North Platte, is the largest railroad <a href="/wiki/Classification_yard" title="Classification yard">classification yard</a> in the world. The route of the <a href="/wiki/First_Transcontinental_Railroad" title="First Transcontinental Railroad">original transcontinental railroad</a> runs through the state.</p>
<p>Other major railroads with operations in the state are: <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BNSF" title="BNSF">BNSF Railway</a>; <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Railway" title="Canadian National Railway">Canadian National Railway</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Iowa_Interstate_Railroad" title="Iowa Interstate Railroad">Iowa Interstate Railroad</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_highways">Roads and highways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Roads and highways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Nebraska's government operates under the framework of the Nebraska Constitution, adopted in 1875,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and is divided into three branches: executive, legislative, and judicial.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Nebraska" title="Governor of Nebraska">Governor of Nebraska</a></div>
<p>The head of the executive branch is <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Nebraska" title="Governor of Nebraska">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Pete_Ricketts" title="Pete Ricketts">Pete Ricketts</a>. Other elected officials in the executive branch are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Nebraska" title="Lieutenant Governor of Nebraska">Lieutenant Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Foley_(Nebraska_politician)" title="Mike Foley (Nebraska politician)">Mike Foley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Attorney_General" title="Nebraska Attorney General">Attorney General</a> <a href="/wiki/Doug_Peterson_(politician)" title="Doug Peterson (politician)">Doug Peterson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Nebraska" title="Secretary of State of Nebraska">Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_A._Gale" title="John A. Gale">John A. Gale</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Treasurer" title="State Treasurer">State Treasurer</a> <a href="/wiki/Don_Stenberg" title="Don Stenberg">Don Stenberg</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Auditor" title="State Auditor">State Auditor</a> <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Janssen" title="Charlie Janssen">Charlie Janssen</a>. All elected officials in the executive branch serve four-year terms.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Legislature" title="Nebraska Legislature">Nebraska Legislature</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_State_Capitol" title="Nebraska State Capitol">Nebraska State Capitol</a></div>
<p>Nebraska is the only state in the United States with a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> legislature. Although this house is officially known simply as the "<a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Legislature" title="Nebraska Legislature">Legislature</a>", and more commonly called the "Unicameral", its members call themselves "senators". Nebraska's Legislature is also the only <a href="/wiki/State_legislature_(United_States)" title="State legislature (United States)">state legislature</a> in the United States that is officially <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nonpartisan_system" title="Nonpartisan system">nonpartisan</a>. The senators are elected with no party affiliation next to their names on the ballot, and members of any party can be elected to the positions of speaker and committee chairs. The Nebraska Legislature can also override the governor's veto with a three-fifths majority, in contrast to the two-thirds majority required in some other states.</p>
<p>The Legislature meets in the third <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_State_Capitol" title="Nebraska State Capitol">Nebraska State Capitol</a> building, built between 1922 and 1932. It was designed by <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Goodhue" title="Bertram Goodhue">Bertram G. Goodhue</a>. Built from Indiana limestone, the capitol's base is a cross within a square. A 400-foot domed tower rises from this base. The Sower, a 19-foot bronze statue representing agriculture, crowns the building. When Nebraska became a state in 1867, its legislature consisted of two houses: a House of Representatives and a Senate. For years, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/George_W._Norris" title="George W. Norris">George Norris</a> and other Nebraskans encouraged the idea of a unicameral legislature, and demanded the issue be decided in a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a>. Norris argued:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>The constitutions of our various states are built upon the idea that there is but one class. If this be true, there is no sense or reason in having the same thing done twice, especially if it is to be done by two bodies of men elected in the same way and having the same jurisdiction.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Unicameral supporters also argued that a <a href="/wiki/Bicameralism" title="Bicameralism">bicameral</a> legislature had a significant undemocratic feature in the committees that reconciled House and Senate legislation. Votes in these committees were secretive, and would sometimes add provisions to bills that neither house had approved. Nebraska's unicameral legislature today has rules that bills can contain only one subject, and must be given at least five days of consideration. In 1934, due in part to the budgetary pressure of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, Nebraska citizens ran a state initiative to vote on a constitutional amendment creating a unicameral legislature, which was approved, which, in effect, abolished the House of Representatives (the lower house).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Judicial branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Supreme_Court" title="Nebraska Supreme Court">Nebraska Supreme Court</a></div>
<p>The judicial system in Nebraska is unified, with the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Supreme_Court" title="Nebraska Supreme Court">Nebraska Supreme Court</a> having administrative authority over all the courts within the state. Nebraska uses the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Plan" title="Missouri Plan">Missouri Plan</a> for the selection of judges at all levels, including <a href="/wiki/County_court#United_States" title="County court">county courts</a> (as the lowest-level courts) and twelve <a href="/wiki/District_court#United_States" title="District court">district courts</a>, which contain one or more counties. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nebraska_State_Court_of_Appeals" title="Nebraska State Court of Appeals">Nebraska State Court of Appeals</a> hears appeals from the district courts, <a href="/wiki/Juvenile_court" title="Juvenile court">juvenile courts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Workers%27_compensation" title="Workers' compensation">workers' compensation</a> courts, and is the final court of appeal.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal_government_representation">Federal government representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Federal government representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="819" data-file-width="1024" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg/220px-Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg/330px-Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg/440px-Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nebraska_State_Capitol_Highsmith.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_State_Capitol" title="Nebraska State Capitol">Nebraska State Capitol</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_Nebraska" title="Lincoln, Nebraska">Lincoln, Nebraska</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/United_States_congressional_delegations_from_Nebraska" title="United States congressional delegations from Nebraska">United States congressional delegations from Nebraska</a></div>
<p>Nebraska's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">U.S. senators</a> are <a href="/wiki/Deb_Fischer" title="Deb Fischer">Deb Fischer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ben_Sasse" title="Ben Sasse">Ben Sasse</a>, both Republicans; Fischer, elected in 2012, is the senior.</p>
<p>Nebraska has three representatives in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>: <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Fortenberry" title="Jeff Fortenberry">Jeff Fortenberry</a> (R) of the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Nebraska's 1st congressional district">1st district</a>; <a href="/wiki/Don_Bacon_(politician)" title="Don Bacon (politician)">Don Bacon</a> (R) of the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Nebraska's 2nd congressional district">2nd district</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Adrian_Smith_(politician)" title="Adrian Smith (politician)">Adrian Smith</a> (R) of the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Nebraska's 3rd congressional district">3rd district</a>.</p>
<p>Nebraska is one of two states (<a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">Maine</a> being the other) that allow for a split in the state's allocation of <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electoral votes</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election" title="United States presidential election">presidential elections</a>. Under a 1991 law, two of Nebraska's five votes are awarded to the winner of the statewide popular vote, while the other three go to the highest vote-getter in each of the state's three <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_congressional_districts" title="List of United States congressional districts">congressional districts</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election_in_Nebraska,_2012" title="United States presidential election in Nebraska, 2012">United States presidential election in Nebraska, 2012</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_gubernatorial_election,_2014" title="Nebraska gubernatorial election, 2014">Nebraska gubernatorial election, 2014</a>; <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate_election_in_Nebraska,_2014" title="United States Senate election in Nebraska, 2014">United States Senate election in Nebraska, 2014</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Nebraska" title="Political party strength in Nebraska">Political party strength in Nebraska</a></div>
<p>For most of its history, Nebraska has been a solidly <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> state. Republicans have carried the state in all but one presidential election since <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1940" title="United States presidential election, 1940">1940</a>: the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1964" title="United States presidential election, 1964">1964 landslide election</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">Lyndon B. Johnson</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2004" title="United States presidential election, 2004">2004 presidential election</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> won the state's five electoral votes by a margin of 33 percentage points (making Nebraska's the fourth-strongest Republican vote among states) with 65.9% of the overall vote; only <a href="/wiki/Thurston_County,_Nebraska" title="Thurston County, Nebraska">Thurston County</a>, which is majority-<a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native American</a>, voted for his <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a> challenger <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a>. In <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2008" title="United States presidential election, 2008">2008</a>, the state split its electoral votes for the first time: Republican <a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a> won the popular vote in Nebraska as a whole and two of its three congressional districts; the second district, which includes the city of Omaha, went for Democrat <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.</p>
<p>Despite the current Republican domination of Nebraska politics, the state has a long tradition of electing <a href="/wiki/Centrism" title="Centrism">centrist</a> members of both parties to state and federal office; examples include <a href="/wiki/George_W._Norris" title="George W. Norris">George W. Norris</a> (who served few years in the Senate as an independent), <a href="/wiki/J._James_Exon" title="J. James Exon">J. James Exon</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Bob_Kerrey" title="Bob Kerrey">Bob Kerrey</a>. Voters have tilted to the right in recent years with the election of <a href="/wiki/Conservatism" title="Conservatism">conservative</a> <a href="/wiki/Mike_Johanns" title="Mike Johanns">Mike Johanns</a> to the U.S. Senate and the 2006 re-election of <a href="/wiki/Ben_Nelson" title="Ben Nelson">Ben Nelson</a>, who was considered the most conservative Democrat in the Senate until his retirement in 2013, when he was replaced by conservative Republican <a href="/wiki/Deb_Fischer" title="Deb Fischer">Deb Fischer</a>.</p>
<p>Former President <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Ford" title="Gerald Ford">Gerald Ford</a> was born in Nebraska, but moved away shortly after birth. <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> native <a href="/wiki/William_Jennings_Bryan" title="William Jennings Bryan">William Jennings Bryan</a> represented Nebraska in Congress, served as <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">U.S. Secretary of State</a> under President <a href="/wiki/Woodrow_Wilson" title="Woodrow Wilson">Woodrow Wilson</a>, and unsuccessfully ran for President three times.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="College_sports">College sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: College sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="NCAA_Division_I_sports">NCAA Division I sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nebraska&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: NCAA Division I sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a> has been held in <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha</a> since 1950. It was held at <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Rosenblatt_Stadium" title="Johnny Rosenblatt Stadium">Rosenblatt Stadium</a> from 1950 through 2010, and at <a href="/wiki/TD_Ameritrade_Park_Omaha" title="TD Ameritrade Park Omaha">TD Ameritrade Park Omaha</a> since 2011.</p>
<p>The following are <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division I</a> college sports programs in Nebraska.</p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Category:Nebraska" title="Category:Nebraska">Topics</a></th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="width:1%;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Conflicts</a></th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
